<Author>alw2005
<Content>OK place, but didn't clean my room the first day The hotel is in a good location because it is close to the bioluminescent bay and close to good beaches. It was kind of hard to find because their address did not come up on the GPS, and they did not have directions on their website.We stayed in room 214. It was fine, although the first day we noticed ants on the floor. We stayed three nights. On the first day we were gone all day and came back and our room had not been cleaned. Just after 4pm when we arrived back, a housekeeper came by and asked if we wanted the room cleaned. we had been hiking all day and just wanted to nap, so I sent her away, but it was pretty annoying that the room was not cleaned before 4pm when we returned. The room was cleaned on the 2nd day.They gym is great!We tried to get towels to use to pool but they were out, so we had to go spend $30 at Walgreens on beach towels. Neither the pool nor the front desk had clean towels for us to use. The Mexican restaurant on site was ok. The guidebooks say it's great and that locals come from nearby to eat there, but it was kind of bland and definitely not authentic Mexican. The margaritas were very sugary. We also attempted to try the seafood restaurant on site. We were seated around 8pm and wait for about 20 minutes for someone to take our order. In addition, our order was taken AFTER a couple that arrived AFTER us. We both wanted the sancocho, but they were out of that. My husband wanted one of their pork entrees, but they were also out of that. At that point we decided to leave. We did drive two minutes down the road to Rosa's Seafood, which was AWESOME. We had a great waitress and the food was great and we were taken care of right away. If you stay at Fajardo Inn, you should definitely venture our and go to Rosa's, and NOT eat at the onsite restaurants. There is also a chain restaurant in Fajardo called Pollo Tropical which is very good. Fajardo also has lots of grocery stores which we found to be helpful for cutting costs. We bought breakfast food and ate in our rooms instead of eating out and bought wine/alcohol there to further cut costs. The beach at Luquillo is a must. We spent the day and rented two lounge chairs and an umbrella for $20. There are seafood kiosks and drinks nearby and they are inexpensive. The parking was $3 and a bracelet to use the bathroom all day was $1 per person. We had an awesome day there.

<Author>BlueRidgeBadger
<Content>Affordable and Pleasant for a Brief Stay We spent one night at this hotel between a day trip to El Yunque and a flight to Vieques (we didn't realize when we booked the room that flights were about to move to Ceiba instead of leaving from Fajardo; no problem, though, since it's an easy 10-minute drive). We had no complaints--this more than met our needs for a lazy late afternoon after a long day and before an early morning--but I probably wouldn't plan an extended stay here.Our room was pleasant, and the balcony offered a nice view, but as other reviewers have noted, it's small (maybe 3'x5'?) with no furniture--the kind of place you can stand with one or at most two other people, check out the weather or enjoy the view for 3 or 4 minutes, and return inside. Our king-sized bed was like those in all the other Puerto Rican hotels we stayed at that weren't part of major chains--it wasn't uncomfortable, but it was too soft by most US standards, so while I slept well, I woke up with a stiff back. The room was cheerful, not huge but larger than I expected, with a nice bathroom and spacious shower with adequate water pressure. If you don't usually travel with shampoo, be forewarned that the toiletries included within our room were just soap, bodywash, and body lotion.The staff at the main office was very friendly and helpful. Check-in is at 4pm, but we arrived in town around 2pm and stopped by, hoping we'd be able to at least drop off our luggage before driving around town or heading to the beach. Not only did they allow us to drop off our luggage and do all the check-in except actually get the room key, but we were welcomed to use the facilities: two pools (a smallish one, frequented by adults; and a very large one with a large slide, water games, an area that looked like a 25m-or-close-to-it pool, suitable for laps, as well as what looked like a pool restaurant-bar, though it was unstaffed and unstocked when we were there); a minigolf course; tennis and basketball courts; a large gym with quite a bit of nautilus/weight/exercise equipment; a juice bar; a hair salon; and 2 restaurants (though neither were open in the middle of the day, I don't think). We could stop in and give our names even before we had a room number to give and pick up pool/beach towels, and the pools and gym were free; minigolf was $2/person; I'm not sure about the tennis and basketball. Overall, the room, the grounds and the facilities were much nicer than I had anticipated.We ate dinner and breakfast at Starfish. The dinner menu included several Caribbean options as well as some salmon and other non-local dishes; the breakfast menu was very American. Both meals were pretty good. There's also a Mexican restaurant at the hotel.Hotel negatives: our AC worked, but just barely. It wasn't so hot that we felt like calling maintenance, but if it had been just 5 degrees warmer, this would have been an annoyance. No breakfast included with stay, though the Starfish restaurant on site serves breakfast (eggs or pancakes or french toast plus coffee, juice, bacon or sausage, was about $9; there were cheaper options available). No internet access in the rooms; there's a business center with one computer and a sign instructing you to contact the front desk for internet access--we didn't bother, but I'm assuming it's not free or cheap.Location negatives: This place sort of has the feeling of an aspiring all-inclusive resort, except it most obviously doesn't include the beach. The view if you look out toward the ocean is nice, but if you look straight down at the neighborhood you've passed through on your way to the hotel that sits atop a little hill a few miles inland, there are some industrial buildings and working class neighborhoods and a not particularly picturesque commercial district. The beach is at least a 5-minute drive away, maybe a bit more (we didn't drive directly). Perhaps families with young children would find this resort largely adequate to entertain them for a short vacation, and it would definitely be more affordable than most resorts, but most visitors would probably want to leave and head out elsewhere--the beaches, parks, biobays, etc., which means you'd probably want to rent a car, and you'd need to make arrangements for biobay tours and do other stuff that would be taken care of for you at the larger resorts this place mimics. I'd recommend this place for people spending one or two nights in Fajardo before or after taking the ferry or flight to Vieques or Culebra or for others stopping briefly in the area. I think it would be an easy place to entertain young children, too. But if you're looking for a home base for a week at the beaches in the region, you'd probably prefer a hotel that's actually nearer the beach.

<Author>gatesnyc
<Content>Exceeded expectations My husband and I stayed for 4 nights. The hotel and grounds where very clean and attractive, they have many fruit trees and nicely landscaped grounds. We did not use the pools but relaxed by them one evening and it was great. I recommend this hotel to families with young kids as the pool seems like a great place for them, there were a couple of families using the pools. As we where a bit tired the first night we went to the more expensive restaurant in the hotel grounds, it was ok, but you can find better food for the same price or less outside (Pasion por el Fogon, Calizo, and a restaurant by the Bioluminescent Bay, etc)I also stayed in Passion Fruit bed and breakfast. Passion Fruit was great as well and the service and attention was better and more intimate than Fajardo Inn. Breakfast was very good and the place was very clean. Passion Fruit was a bit nosier in terms of people coming in/out of rooms and all the AC units running created a lot of noise. These are two distinct logging options so comparing them is a bit unfair and it depends if you like a Bed and Breakfast vs. Hotel/Resort accommodations. I will probably not go back to Passion Fruit, depends on the price, etc. I only saved a few dollars in Fajardo Inn vs Passion Fruit, so I think Fajardo Inn is a better bang for the buck.On Fajardo Inn - Negative - 1. We stayed in the 1st floor room and the window overlooks a large common terrace, so not much privacy unless you close the curtains.2. The AC drip caused noise on night #1, as it was hitting the exterior of our room AC. We complained and told them to put a towel out to absorb the noise and the problem was resolved.Positive - 1. <Author>rrzzll
<Content>Service oriented and pleasant staff Nancy B. at the Fajardo Inn worked wonders for us and made our trip a delight.In my opinion Fajardo is a must see destination when visiting Puerto Rico. The reserve at Los Cabezas de San Juan which includes the Fajardo Lighthouse has the most spectacular views in all the island. However, you must make reservations to join the tour and this is where the difficulty comes in. Their reservations # will bring you around in voicemail circles with no way out. Nancy personally made our reservations for us. She also arranged a last minute tour of the Nearby Bio Bay after calling around (no simple thing as these tours are limited and usually sold out on the weekends in high season).The Inn itself is a bit funky and oddly furnished, but very reasonable and clean.Thank you Nancy!

<Author>quivondra
<Content>Decent hotel, great customer service, but don't expect luxury. Upon arriving in Fajardo, I was simply not impressed with the immediate surroundings. It seems this town is a launching pad to see the rainforest and to visit viecques or culebra. My first impression was that the customer service was impeccable. The staff was incredibly friendly and helpful. When I called for towels or pillows, I received them in a timely manner. The honeymoon suite was ok. We had some problems with the door key, but someone came by to fix this issue. The floors are tile and the bathroom is dark with a large tub. It's not hugely luxurious, but clean and sufficient. The kitchen area was a huge plus, since we didn't want to eat out in Fajardo (options were limited) and we certainly didn't want to rely on eating at the on-site restaurants 3x a day. The living area was also decent, however don't expect luxury linens.The grounds were kept up, but there is a lot of construction going on. Also, note that the pool area with mini-golf and tennis courts is open to the public. I did have a good time there for a few days, but as I was on my babymoon, it simply wasn't romantic enough. We checked out a day early when a full bus of local teenagers showed up at the open pool and they started blasting reggaeton. We went to the reception area and booked a room at el convento in old san juan and handed in our keys. All in all, this is a wonderful place in a not-so-amazing area IF you have kids with you. I really wouldn't recommend staying here for romance. After years of trips to mexico, the local beaches just don't compare. I'm sure the surrounding islands are great, but we stood in line for an hour in the morning to get on a ferry. A half hour before departure, they said the tickets had been all sold... and the line had never even moved. I'm a very DIY person and like to rent a car and travel around locally... but in this case, I regret not paying the extra cash to stay in San Juan or elsewhere and just taking proper tours to the islands for snorkeling.  
<Date>Sep 1, 2008

<Author>Jeannie1717
<Content>Nice Place We stayed here for one night on our jaunt through Puerto Rico. The complex is very nice, but a bit hard to find. It is not on the beach and is a little drive to anything else. The rooms were clean, well appointed, but a very small TV for the size of the room. No problems with service or maintenance. The pool area was beautiful, but we weren't here long enough to enjoy it. I would recommend this hotel to anyone looking for relatively inexpensive, clean accommodations in Fajardo. We did take the East Wind bioluminesence tour in the evening that was 109.00 per person. It was well worth the money as it included a catamaran boat ride to Vieques (with rum drinks included), a van ride to dinner (included in price), at a very unique little restaurant, another bus ride (old school bus) to the middle of nowhere- a little scary for some! Then a pontoon boat ride to the bay where you can see and swim with the marvels of nature. Many folks in our group jumped right in and swam with the creatures that make this an ultra unique gift from nature. You can get more info on this at biobay.com Well worth the money. All in all the Fajardo Inn was fine for us. I am a stickler when it comes to cleanliness and this hotel met my demands.

<Author>swansrus2
<Content>A Perfect Hotel We spent three nights wonderful at Fajardo Inn, a charming hill-top hotel that offers spectacular views and exceptional service. The hotel design and landscaping is top-notch and the entire staff is very professional and pleasant. They will provide maps and directions to anywhere you wish to go. Fajardo Inn offers two large heated pools, one of which features a waterfall, slide and jacuzzi, miniature golf, playground and tennis courts,as well as several terraces scattered throughout for lounging. The hotel also provides towels for use at the pools, laundry facilities and internet. The hotel lobby is rather grand and our room was very nicely decorated, offering refrigerator, coffee maker, hairdryer, cable TV and ocean view balcony. The hotel grounds and buildings were immaculate throughout. There are two dining rooms and the food and service in each is great. Fajardo Inn is perfectly located for a trip to Luquillo Beach, El Yunque and the islands of Culebra and Vieques. Spending a few night at Fajardo Inn is a wonderful vacation in itself and is definitely one of the nicest, friendliest and most enjoyable hotels in Puerto Rico. We wish we could have stayed longer.

<Author>caraheartstravel
<Content>Okay stay If I could give the hotel 3.5 stars, I would, but I'll err on the side of caution. I paid about $125/night after taxes for room 132, all the way in the back of the hotel on the first floor.Pros: Very professional and helpful staff (had maps printed for each desination that I inquired about) with a 24 hour desk, nice property, nice, clean pools, large enough grounds to not feel crowded even when the hotel is full. The hotel restaurant (Blue Iguana?) got some flack in previous reviews -- while I would not call it authentic, the prices were decent and the food always filling, not to mention the convenience of having a place to get some quick food right in the hotel. Good-sized room, well-kept property. Convenient to Seven Seas beach and highway 3 to get to El Yunque/any points south.Cons: I'm generally not a picky hotel customer, but for the price, there were several small problems that I might have ignored had the hotel been cheaper. Doors to the outside were left open at all hours of the day, and cleaning staff left the room doors open while cleaning -- this resulted in an army of mosquitos in the room each night, and fresh bites each morning. Bathroom had a slight smell, maybe mold. The door/lock was smaller than the frame, which led to a banging sound all night long as the door rattled with the breeze -- to accompany the knocking sound in the a/c. Two days into the trip our cards randomly did not work for the room, although the desk was quick to replace them. In an effort to tidy up the room, the housekeeping staff occasionally stuck things in random drawers/out of sight, which meant some hunting around to find things.All in all, as a bargain traveler, I might look for a cheaper hotel next time instead of paying for the nice facilities, which we rarely used (there's too much else to do!). If you're looking for a more relaxed vacation where you plan to spend a bulk of your time at the hotel, or for an extended business stay, this is probably a suitable place.

<Content>Excellent Value! When we arrived in the Fajardo area, we went past the small sign that said Inn. The Inn is in a great location once you realize it is on the hill. We only stayed the night, however, the check in service was great. The staff over extended themselves in order to ensure we were comfortable. They even checked my flight for me, to see if it was leaving on time. We were there on a Saturday, when we arrived we had the front desk book a tour for us at the bioluminous Bay. We went kayaking at night. Try to pre book; we got the last two spots. The area where you kayak has several little shack like restaurants. Lively music was playing every where. It was quite the experience to kayak through the canals into the bay. The trip was $40.00 approx. The restaurant at the Fajardo Inn was having a rough time Sunday morning, half their staff didn't show up. Needless to say I drank several cups of coffee and no breaky! We didnt' get a chance to get to the beach around there, however, we went for a quick dip in the pool. Amazing, they had a few different pools, one I had to myself to do laps. Their gym facilities had very updated equipment. Things to consider:-there is no elevator and it is very steep; not appropriate for seniors or disabled unless you get ground level-rooms were adequate; mattress too soft-clean-several families there; obviously a popular place for the locals to holiday as well. ***Rented from Charlie Car rental excellent value and great service.

<Author>motown47
<Content>LOVED the Fajardo Inn! I am shocked to read the previous review. If it is from a recent visit, (first weekend in April) I might have been there at the same time. Doesn't even seem like the same place!First of all, the staff was amazing. Everyone did everything possible to make this a great stay. From providing maps, directions, food tips, etc. I found each and every staff member to be top of the line. The manager...I think her name was MarieLynn or something like that-- was particularly kind to my family. I was with my elderly mother and sister and she came and sat and talked with us all about Fajardo and gave us some interesting details of life in Puerto Rico. Cleanliness: top notch. We had a triple room-three double beds-which is a first for us. The room was immaculate. The floor was stone tiles and and the housekeeper mopped the floors every day. The hallways were also mopped daily. I was particularly surprised one night to leave the room around 9 PM and a housekeeper was quietly polishing all of the furniture in the parlor. Sheets were changed daily which has not been the case in many hotels I have visited recently. Food: okay, the Starfish restaurant on the premises was not that great. My mother had fried shrimp which was entirely overcooked. BUT....when we told the waiter he not only brought her a new order, he did not charge for the wine my sister and I were enjoying. The Mexican restaurant on site was really good. And once again, I must disagree with a previous reviewer. We found the prices to be extremely reasonable. Large chicken nacho platter WITH two sodas came to about $7.00. I have paid double that for the platter alone. There are several small places on the road to the Inn which are quite good. The pools are beautiful. Very quiet. If you want the cabana guys and pina coladas delivered poolside, this is not the place. It's the place to read a book. We didn't even see Coco's park until the second day. What a place for kids! Miniature golf, basketball, and incredible pools. We swam and sunbathed in the quiet pool right outside our room. (use lots of sunscreen..that sun is pretty intense).Anyway, our visit to the Fajardo Inn was a huge success. Again, I must issue one caveat. If you want action, noise, music, etc. this is not the place. It is a place to relax in a beautiful environment. I would not hesistate to recommend this place!

<Author>mcl9699
<Content>Just what we were looking for! I was a little hesitant after reading such varied reviews and also that the hotel wasn't on the beach, but we tried it anyway. We were very pleasantly rewarded!We found the hotel very easy to find - followed the directions on the hotel website and got there on the first try! It was a great drive from the San Juan airport - very scenic. Our check in went smoothly and we were in our room in no time. The room was beautiful - tile floors, a wooden sleigh bed, beautiful tv console... The balcony was a little small, but easy for two to stand outside and gaze at the ocean in the distance. We had the door open alot in the daytime to let fresh air in. There were screens in the windows, so we had them open all the time, too. We wanted to get as much warm air as possible, coming from winter in PA! The in room safe was big enough for my husband's laptop (and still had more room). The bedding was comfy, and there was a coffeemaker and a refrigerator, so we bought our own water bottles and drinks... The bathroom was fantastic. There was no mold or mildew and everything was very updated and modern. The soaps even smelled awesome! The tiled shower was HUGE - no bathtub, though. Housekeeping kept the room very clean. The pool was amazing - all tile and looked like it was recently remodeled. Never anyone there during our stay. There was a section for laps, a section with a basketball hoop, a slide, and the zero entry point. A GREAT pool for all ages - lots of shallow water yet lots for adults too. Didn't do the mini golf but it looked nice - $2 extra to try it. Pool was open 8am to 9pm, and a smaller pool was open from 9am to 10pm. This smaller pool was closer to the hotel rooms and was also very beautiful. lots of changing rooms - we checked out then hung out by the pool because of our later flight. Staff was extremely nice and accomodating. Requests for extra towels were taken care of immediately. Hotel grounds were beautiful and very clean and well taken care of. Playground looked nice and aviary was cool, too. The only bad was the restaurants. We only ate at the mexican one and it was nothing special... beef was very chewy...overpriced... Don't waste your time eating there... breakfast and lunch? go the the Golden Bakery right down the street - less than half a mile before the hotel - great food!!! and cheap! and for a beach - go to seven seas beach about 10 minutes drive from the hotel. we went there three times and were always the only ones there. The water was clear and calm - nicer than the other beaches we went to like Luquillo. Go to Culebra and rent a jeep for $130 for the day and beach hop there!!! We went to Zoni - nice, but Flamenco was gorgeous! This hotel was great because of it's location - we always stay on the beach previously so it was a gamble for me, but i loved being close to the ferry - we were late one morning and drove there and parked and got on the ferry in 5 minutes! We were there for 5 nights and it was quiet the whole time - we seldom saw any other guests! Only good food we found was the Kiosk - was it 2 or 12? in Luquillo - go through the dumpy front part and there's a great section on the beach in the back.

<Author>DCChiq
<Content>Good for a short stay Duration of stay: one nightThis is the about the best you'll get for something in the $130/night range. I like that location was situated right in the middle of town. It never felt unsafe and it was easy to get around (via taxi). Staff service was good. They were quick to jump on whatever we needed. It did feel a little dead which I thought was strange for March but then again, we stayed Sunday to Monday and Sunday is typically a very slow night in Puerto Rico. THINGS WE LOVED:*Great location*Very spacious, never crowded*Rooms were spotless*Several pools*The inn had a really nice humble and sincere vibe to it*Prompt service by the staff. Example: We asked for a cab, they called him immediately, he knew most of the staff on site so we felt comfortable with him taking us wherever, he took us to the restaurant and then returned to pick us up and bring us back (and didn't charge us until the cab back home), and gave us a small tour of the town on the way back.*A lot to do on the grounds*State of the art gym with top quality equipment*Great place to order smoothies by the gym*Good quality samples in the bathroom (shampoo, conditioner, lotion)*Coffee maker in room; good coffee to go with it*Great views from the balconyTHINGS THAT COULD'VE BEEN BETTER:*The on site food restaurants. They were average at best. Venture out - much better in the area. NOTE: if you ask the staff, make sure you ask specifically for what you want in your dining experience. For example, we said we wanted great authentic quality food and we were sent to a restaurant in a sketchier part of town (Rosa's which was EXCELLENT) where you had to be buzzed in. Don't get me wrong - the food was great and we would go there again since we can adjust to anything and we didn't mind at all about the location, however, what we had in mind was more of a place for good scenery where we could lounge outdoors by the ocean, etc. *The pool bar was abandoned. What a waste of revenue opportunity! This place has so much potential. The pool bar was built in with a grill and NO ONE was working it. It was just abandoned and run down. How can the owner let something like that go to waste on a such gorgeous piece of land?! Alcohol  food are a huge source of revenue -and you'd think this would be OPEN and upkept. My first thought was, maybe their fridge or something is open - but then I thought, they should bring down a cooler and make some money or at least have a waiter/waitress from the bar nearby take drink/food orders. I couldn't understand how this was just let go and not cared for.Overall, it's a good bang for your dollar. I recommend this inn for a shorter stay.

<Author>cyasukot
<Content>A Bit Sad . . . We stayed for two days while exploring El Yunke before going off to Vieques. The Hotel is serviceable, but it seems like it's seen better days. The restaurant fare is microwaved and dinner at the Starfish (the onsite restaurant) had terrible service and food and ambiance reminiscent of a airport lounge late at night. Everything you want comes at an extra price (exercise room, internet) and there are draconian rules in effect at the pool, whose swim up bar featured in their brochure no longer exists (the seats are still there, and a half torn down tiki hut sits sadly on the cement, but it is not functional and no staff are around the pool to help with any requests). There is no collection of brochures for local dining or attractions, so you're on your own. We got lost at night in a slightly alarming neighborhood foraging for food. We finally found the Metropol restaurant the next day and had a good meal there - wish this type of local dining had been available at the hotel. Front desk staff was helpful when asked, but seemed more oriented towards checking people in and out. Room was a bit musty and strangely, the shower has no ledge for your bathing products even though it was gargantuan in size.

<Author>IndyMary41
<Content>The Inn good, the setting bad... Pros: Beautiful, well maintained, scenic facilities, Friendly and helpful staff, Clean rooms.Cons: Location and surrounding streets and neighborhood, security questions, overcharged based on menu prices at restaurants, fees for use of the fitness facility. The Inn was a very nice place. I want to begin this review with the major issues we had, however. Our priorities were safety and ease of getting around since the Inn is tucked away from other tourist-type destinations. Please read on, though, to the positives of the Inn, if my stated concerns are not high on your personal priority list. I agree with previous reviews that state it is not in a good location. It sits near industrial sites and a run-down community. Traffic problems and poverty abound in the vicinity. Of course, this is not the inn's fault, but travelers should beware if these are the issues that concern them:  First-Although we experienced no direct threats to our security, the grounds of Fajardo Inn are not gated and we saw no evidence of on-site security....? Secondary entrance doors were left standing open during the day.  Second-Driving to and from the Inn was treacherous! Streets near the Inn were very rough, with large potholes and traffic was very congested at times. If you plan to drive around Fajardo and Puerto Rico at all, note that the driving of locals is very unpredictable and wreckless by U.S. standards. Rules at stop lights are disregarded (stopping seems to be more of a suggestion), drivers cut others off on the thoroughfares and at corners. They are impatient, regularly laying on the horn and waving their hands in the air at other drivers! On Sunday of our visit, there were many people riding horseback on the streets (during the day and in the dark), blocking traffic, darting across in front of automobiles (at one location, with the horses tied up, the people sat in the roadways in the dark. This made even the safest driving hazardous). At the major intersection nearest the Inn, a local was approaching the car and panhandling daily.  The Inn itself is not a bad place, however. The facility itself was beautiful, with breath-taking views. The rooms were very clean and supplied daily (complimentary coffee,soaps, shampoo, conditioner, and lotion). The staff was friendly and accommodating. The pools were clean and inviting.The food at the Blue Iguana was good, while the Star Fish was fair. Service in both restaurants was average.  *Beware, however, that we were consistently overcharged on meals, drinks, etc. When we pointed this out, the response was that the menu prices need updating. (This seemed to be a trend, as the same thing happened at the highly recommended Rosa's). We found that the local restaurants in general were overrated, lacking high quality service and/or pleasant fine dining atmosphere as ratings suggest. We came to believe that ratings were likely based on comparisions with other local establishments. We did not utilize the fitness facility, due to the fact there was an $5 fee for each session. On a final note, I read another reviewer's comment that plumbing was not functioning properly. We experienced that also.

<Author>ElGringoViajero
<Content>Has much potential, but needs to work on details I stayed at the Fajardo Inn for the last two nights of a trip to Puerto Rico. The hotel is in the coastal city of Fajardo. The best way to summarize this hotel is that it is nice, but needs to work on some details. The directions I was given were not that great and it was hard to find. The hotel is just off Route 195. Once you get off of Route 3 at the 195 exit, Route 195 breaks up after a short distance and the signage is not great in terms of helping you find where it picks up again. The hotel does look quite attractive from the outside. The parking at the hotel is a bit of a challenge since the road is narrow and part of it is on gravel. The hotel staff members at the registration desk were pleasant and gave me an electronic card key for my room. The elevator was out of service so I carried my bags upstairs. I later noticed a sign saying that baggage assistance was available, but the sign had been partially blocked by a plant. I left the hotel the next day at 8am. When I returned at 4:30pm, my room had not been made up. Ten minutes later, I heard a knock at the door and the maid wanted to make up my room. I asked why she hadn't serviced the room earlier and she said she had 30 rooms to cover. I declined the service since I didn't want to leave my room again. By the way, there is no peep hole in the door which is a security risk. In terms of the room, the bed was quite comfortable and the furnishings were nice. The lamps in the room had 3-way switches but the bulbs were the newer energy-efficient bulbs that didn't work well with the 3-way switches. The bathroom had some oddities. There is no hair dryer. Ordinarily I wouldn't care, but hair dryers were an advertised feature. Also, there is strangely no place to put your soap or shampoo when you are in the shower. I kept looking for a soap dish but could not find one. There were two bath towels, but only one washcloth. In terms of the hotel features, I wanted to use the pool but for some reason it closes at 7pm. This is way too early for a pool to close. The room did have an electronic safe - a nice addition if you are using a laptop. I would be willing to stay there again. This hotel has so much potential if it could just work on some of the details.

<Author>emperorprince
<Content>Great Choice To Stay Here From the moment I arrived at the Fajardo Inn, everyone was extremely welcoming and very nice and accomodating. The hotel was spotless and they had an adorable christmas tree and village setup in the main staircase. I loved it. My room was perfectly clean and the bed was amazingly comfortable. When I stepped out on to my balcony, I had a 180 degree view from the beautiful beach of Fajardo all the way around to El Yunque rainforest. The facilities of the hotel were great, as well. The pool was beautiful every single day and I watched so many families out playing miniature golf. I was able to continue my workouts in their great gym. The staff was always very courteous and polite and my room was spotless every single day. Out in the front waiting area, there were always people just hanging out and laughing with their coffee...just having a good time. The surroundings of the hotel were beautiful. Great landscaping and wild iguanas to lay with you by the pool! At night, the coquis virtually surround the hotel and you can hear them for miles! They almost sing you to sleep. The only thing was the construction going on in a small area in the parking lot, but that is unavoidable. I absolutely loved this place and if I am in Puerto Rico again will DEFINITELY choose the Fajardo Inn. Thank you so much for a wonderful stay.

<Author>bilawing
<Content>A hotel that can't figure out what it wants to be We spent one night at the Fajardo Inn. The stay was adequate but probably not ideal for us. It seems to pitch itself as an inexpensive all-inclusive resort, with putt-putt course, multiple swimming pools, etc; but while the amenities are very family friendly, the environment is more upscale, with no coffee maker in room, and on-site meal costs not inexpensive. Internet was a real pain, with wireless in the lobby, but with generally 30 minutes of struggling to get in!Parking was weird. The lobby is at the top of a hill, surrounded by no parking signs, meaning that a long walk was required just to check in; parking for upper-floor rooms is extremely inconvenient, with many steps.There is a major fudge factor regarding the ocean view. Mountains, yes, but the ocean is somewhat obscured by several blocks of buildings between the hotel and the ocean.Rooms were very attractive and well appointed.

<Author>toonjie
<Content>Fajardo's Sin I was hoping the Fajardo Inn would be a wonderful, lesser known gem that would save big bucks over the Westin and El Conquistador- It did save money, but the savings wasn't worth it! I read a review here that stated the Fajardo Inn is a 2 star hotel with a 5 star pool and that is just about right, only the 5 star pool has some major defects. Let's start with the pool. First, the whole property is very hilly and I wouldn't recommend it for anyone handicapped or who can't walk up steep inclines. The main pool is at the bottom of the hill, so a good walk from most rooms. Most of the pool is only 2 feet deep so you have to walk around 50 feet into the pool before you can actually swim. The swim up bar was not in service while we were there except to feed the 75-100 screaming camp kids that were there using the pool. There was also extrememly loud music blaring the whole time we were there. We had a so-called honeymoon suite, which was a slightly bigger room with a bigger bath with a jaquzzi, only, (major sin), the jaquzzi only holds 1 person-come on, in a honeymoon suite!!!??? Rooms are recently remodeled, but the workmanship is lousy. You could pass an envelope between the seems of the window in our bathroom out to the stairway- no caulk, no wonder so many complain about ants, although we didn't have any. Service throughout was poor, especially for a small hotel and workers simply went through the motions and weren't very friendly. The landscaping is lovely and the property could be a very good one, but the aforementioned sins of a small inn make dropping the big bucks on the Westin the best option in this area for a relaxing luxury stay. The Fajardo Inn is also a good 20 minute drive to the rain forest. In summary these are the cardinal sins- the best feature, the pool has glaring design defects and they have sold out to summer camps to make money, totally ruining the atmosphere for guests, service is poor and unfriendly, which is the chief sin for a small inn in my book. Landscaping is nice but it is very hilly and not for people who can't walk well. Rooms are remoldeled with poor craftsmanship and decor is well, let's say 4 dogs playing poker class of art, etc. Inn is too far from Rain forest and best beach (Loquillo) and in a dumpy neighborhood. Oh, and as mentioned in many reviews, signage is horrific getting to the hotel. We all wished we had spent more money and gone to the Westin.  
<Date>Jul 31, 2007

When we went to use the pool only 2 people were allowed to use the pool and the additoinal person my 3 year would have to pay 21 dollars per day in order to use the facilities (mini golf, pool, ect) or I would have to book an additonal room and spend the night away from my family. So if you arrive let say at 6:00PM and the pool closes at 8:00PM you still have to pay 21 dollars for the use of the pool... $21 dollars for 2 hours is quite expensive plus $21 for every additonal day. As a consumer these rules are ridiculous. When talking to the hotel Manager the first words out of her mouth were NO you may not use the pool unless you pay the aditional fee weather its 2 hours or the full day you still have to pay for the 3rd person. In my opinion no minor child should have to pay an additonal $21 fee to use the pool especially a daily fee - one of the reasons for choosing this hotel was becaus our son loves the pool. On our second stay we stayed from Sat thru Mon. Sat and Sunday we went out on our boat so we did no use the ameneties. On monday we planed to spend the afternoon at the pool. Check out was at 11:00AM... so we Had breakfest at there restaurant and check out and planed to use the pool for the remaining of the afternoon because well we promised our 3 year old that we would take him to the pool. When we went to pool again we were told we could use the pool not because of the $21 fee but becuase you are no longer alowed to use the pool or any of the hotel amenities once you have check out or before you have checked in. Again we talked with the hotel Manager (VERY RUDE and UNPROFESIONAL LADY)... Her very first words were NO - NO you may not use the pool if you have check out of the hotel. Bare in mind, if you stay for one night and you plan to use the pool and lets say you arrive and 4:00PM (Check in Time) you may use the pool and hotel amenities from 4:00PM to 8:00AM on the arrival day and from 8:00AM to 11:00Am on the following day. Dont plan to stay the full day because they will literally kick you out of the hotel / pool and any other amenities they offer.It was very disapointing experience for me and my familiy and i will never use this hotel again unless these new policies are revised. It's a shame becuase the hotel is quite cozy and has an execellent pool but the hotel management and new policies and rules can make your stay a very regretfull experience.A MayorBayamon, PR

<Content>so-so Just stayed at the fajardo inn June 10-12. This hotel is clean and basic, not 5 star by any means.First the bad: Bathrooms are small and they never leave was any wash cloths. Hallways are hot  humid no air conditioning in halls and exit doors are left open. Only 1 ice machine which coincidentally never worked(had to go to restaurant if you wanted ice. Good place to go if your looking to save some money and see the island. Not a good place to stay if your looking to be catered to.

<Content>Very nice and extremely clean resort for the money PROS.... Hotel is extremely clean and it's grounds beaufifully landscaped with all variety of flowers and tropical plants. The room with a balcony is a most, great view of the ocean and the surroundings. The personnel was friendly and helpful. <Content>Good value for the area We stayed at the Fajardo Inn for 2 nights booking 1 room each for 2 couples.The other couple wanted to spend less so we opted for the Fajardo Inn which is not on the beach but 10 minutes or so away.For the price, it is really a great value.The El Conquistador is much nicer and more luxurious but much more expensive.Some of the other reviewers did not have some items in their rooms, but we did.We had a coffee maker,hair dryer,iron, soap,etc.Our room did have a king size bed with extra pillows.The view was not great, but it matched the price.The floors are all tile and the maids clean them daily but I found a mat outside the room would have kept alot of dirt from being tracked in.I was annoyed by it and did wear my socks in the room to keep the dirt off my feet.Our room was very large and the furnishings were nice.The bathroom  shower(no tub) were small and did lack robe hooks,etc.There was only 1 towel bar.There was a dispenser in the shower with shower gel  shampoo.The pools are both really nice and there is even putt putt($3.00 I think.)There is a waterslide  small lazy river type area.It is really great for kids.There were always plenty of chairs open.The hotel is not in a resort type place but after we were there a night we did not mind.Seven Seas beach is about 10 minutes away and Luquillo about 20 minutes.We looked at these beaches and thought they were very dirty and gross.Take the ferry to Culebra for the day for the best beaches in the Caribbean.Playa Flamenco  the others are the best.There are a stray cats  dogs around the hotel( and all of PRico.)I bought pet food at the grocery store in Fajardo and fed them daily while there.We did not eat at the hotel.We ate at the Golden Bagel for breakfast  lunch.We tried Rosa's seafood for dinner 1 night.It was good,not fabulous, but good.I would eat there again.The flan was very good.We also ate at Restaurant Pasion something on the road towards the marina,Seven Seas beach,  the El Conquistador.It is on the left as you go up a hill.It was fabulous.Excellent service.Great skirt steak with tamarind sauce.Great fresh fish and shrimp.Yummy desserts.We have been to Puerto Rico quite a few times and have stayed in Old San Juan,Rincon,Culebra,etc.This trip was not about the beach for us- we were visting friends in Cayey-so we did not have to stay in a beach front resort.If you can stay at a really nice beach front resort, then do it.If you need to watch your money,stay at the Fajardo Inn.It is really a very beautiful property-similar to a better Holiday or Hampton Inn.It is very close to alot of things.The area around the hotel looks run down, but it isn't really.The people around the area are all different types of people.It is not a slum.Puerto Rican houses are different than American houses- they have flat roofs because of hurricanes,etc  most do have ornate iron gates  fences so it is more difficult to see people in their yard,etc.I did enjoy my stay at the hotel.

<Author>Etoile983
<Content>Just OK This hotel is OK for the price. But, I would recommend staying at the El Conquistador, which is only a little bit more expensive (depending on the season). The staff isn't exactly helpful, and the location is only so-so. If you visit Fajardo, definitely invest in a trip to the Biobay. I recommend Capitan Suarez, who does a boat tour. If you kayak into the biobay, the kayaking takes up more of your trip than spending time in the biobay. If you go in via boat, you get to spend much more time swimming in the water, which is a very special and unique experience. Plus, Capitan Suarez talks about the area and the creatures that you encounter during the tour, things you might not notice on your own. Fajardo is fabulous, and is well worth the trip, no matter where you stay.

<Author>Cachalot
<Content>Extremely Disappointing We stayed at the Farjardo Inn for 5 nights beginning 4/15. First the O.K. stuff: The hotel had some plusses: landscaping, 2 nice pools, and if you鈥檙e lucky a good enough room with a good enough view. (I鈥檒l explain more later--but in the meantime don鈥檛 stay in Rm. #208.) Most of the staff were friendly, polite and responsive about requests. The food was O.K. in the Starfish Restaurant. As a whole we found the Puerto Rican people to be very nice.Now the unfortunate minuses. For the life of us we cannot understand why there has been no mention that this hotel, while very nice from the look of it despite it鈥檚 hilly terrain, hammering and sawing noises from a construction project on the property, inconsistencies with pool and restaurant hours, internet use and access problems, hotel amenities not available, a lack of knowledge about reputable and decent resources available to visit the sights, stray dogs and cats in the most pathetic condition about the premises--it has not been mentioned that the location of this hotel is among impoverished and dilapidated neighborhoods and from the looks of what serves as 鈥渉omes鈥?with jail bars or cages around them, some serious crime issues. Although we did not encounter any conflicts in the day during our travels, we guessed that it might have been a different issue at night. The towns are dirty with many boarded-up store fronts and many indigent people idling about the streets or in bars. The Kiosks are disgusting. We can鈥檛 believe why anyone would take a chance at these places. When we asked for a restaurant recommendation, we were told to try Rosa鈥檚 Seafood. As with most everywhere else we drove to, you had to drive through some of the worst poverty stricken neighborhoods we have ever seen. With this place, though, the restaurant was right in the slum with a stripped down car across the street as an added visual treat. How can you enjoy yourself and supposedly enjoy eating a good meal, when you see all the poverty surrounding you? People and animals living in the same squalid conditions just outside as you are stuffing yourself.Are the people at the hotel oblivious or does everyone just accept the terrible conditions of their neighbors? There seems to be no humane services for man or beast. Before entering a Carvel on Rt. 3, we had to be buzzed in. The same for a Radio Shak store. No doubt others. In the parking lots of strip malls, there often is a guard in an elevated tower. If you go to Seven Seas Beach, one side of the road is a beach and the other side a slum again. This is typical of the whole area. If you have to stay in this section of Puerto Rico for some reason, the Fajardo Inn will do, but we found it difficult to enjoy what beauty there is when you have seen the poverty that is between you and some of the beautiful views.

<Content>Monrovia, CA - Relaxing at the Farjardo Inn We stayed at the Fajardo Inn for 2 nights. The staff was helpful and friendly. <Author>tonymMinneapolis
<Content>Good Hotel and Grounds My family stayed at the Fajardo Inn from April 2 to 6, 2007. We had an excellent time exploring the surrounding area, and the Fajardo Inn was a nice place to stay in the area. It is economical and although it is not on the ocean, it has excellent clean swimming pools for the kids. We enjoyed a short drive to nearby beaches, Luquillo and Playa Azul in particular. The Fajardo Inn was clean, spacious and the staff was helpful. The 2 restaurants on site were nothing to brag about, but they were ok and provided a convenient meal when needed. The food was acceptable. If you are looking for the all-inclusive, on the ocean style resort, the Fajardo is not for you. But, if you want to save a lot of money and still stay at a nice, clean place that is conveniently located and that offers good swimming pools for the kids, I would recommend the Fajardo Inn. We would definitely go back, if we return to Puerto Rico.

<Author>chickiewv
<Content>Lots of Basics Missing at Fajardo Inn My best friend and I, both seasoned travelers, stayed at the Fajardo Inn for three nights on our first trip to Puerto Rico last week. We knew it was not on the beach, so that wasn't a disappointment. The rates were good, and it seemed to be a good base of operations for us. The first impression was positive: The front desk staff was quite friendly, and our room was clean, quiet, spacious and comfortable, with nice heavy wood furniture. But it's a pain to lug heavy bags up the staircase; there is no elevator. And after a few hours, you start to notice that a lot of very basic things are missing.  The bathrooms, for example, have no towel hooks or racks to hang wet towels, and there is only one tiny shelf on which to place toiletries. We also asked the front desk for a hair dryer but were told they are all out. Nor was there any sort of clock in our room. Another strange thing: We asked housekeeping for extra towels and washcloths, since we were two active women with many outings a day. We got the towels, but for the duration of our stay, the staff would only provide one single washcloth. I was forced to try to wash with a hand towel. That was ridiculous. To my mind, any decent property manager would spend the $30 or $40 per room to add these items, all of which should be considered even for a two-star property. If I were a manager and someone needed a hair dryer, I'd send them down to the nearest Walgreen's (a few minutes away) to buy one for $10. Failing to supply washcloths, clocks and the like is just lazy. (Speaking of Walgreen's ... this is THE place to go for cheap beach towels, bamboo beach mats, souvenir T-shirts and a good selection of post cards.) I agree with another reviewer who found the property oddly vacant. There seemed to be very few employees working, except for the overworked few at the front desk. The pool bar was never staffed, and the restaurants opened very late in the day. We didn't eat at either, partly for that reason. Also strangely empty were the ice machines and all of the vending machines. There was no bottled water, soda or snacks anywhere in sight. Again, these seems fairly basic. Why have machines if you aren't going to fill them? And ice?!? Come on. We weren't asking for a lot -- just the basics. We had a lot of questions for the front desk, such as directions to restaurants and how to arrange tours of the bioluminescent bay, and everyone who helped us there was knowledgeable and super-friendly. This staff is one of the best things about the hotel. But we found ourselves wondering why they didn't write up little sheets on the most common questions or post the information on their Web site. It would be a nice service for travelers and take some of the load off the overburdened desk staff. A few recommendations about the area:  _The bioluminescent bay, accessible by tours that depart from Las Croabas, 15 mins from Fajardo, is a MUST-DO. Seeing the phytoplankton glow in the dark is absolutely amazing. But be warned: DO NOT ATTEMPT THIS UNLESS YOU ARE AN EXPERIENCED KAYAKER. Fighting the incoming tide and maneuvering in pitch-black darkness through a narrow channel lined with mangrove roots is very scary and challenging. It's not a tour for small children, first-time paddlers or those who frighten easily. However, there are only five places in the world you can see this rare spectacle, and it's worth the $45 to try. _The Caribbean National Forest at El Yunque is also a must-do. We hiked the moderately challenging Big Tree Trail for about 40 minutes to reach La Mina waterfall and had a wonderful afternoon. The falls were crowded, but the water was lovely and worth the walk. The hike back was easier, with less climbing. _The Golden Bagel, just down the hill and maybe a half-mile from the hotel lobby, is the best deal in town for breakfast. Killer bagels, French toast and coffee for rock-bottom prices.  _If you are thinking of taking the ferry to Vieques or Culebra, BUY YOUR TICKETS IN ADVANCE. We didn't know this was an option or we would have done it. We planned to go to Culebra and arrived at the ferry terminal more than 90 minutes before the departure time to buy tickets. We stood in a line that never moved for more than an hour. Seriously. The same guy stood at the front of the line the entire time and never got sold a ticket. As it became apparent there was a problem, I went to the front of the line and discovered that the ferry was boarding all the people who had bought tickets in advance first. Then, if there was room, they would sell more tickets. We decided to jump out of line and buy tickets to Vieques instead, where we spent a nice quiet afternoon on the beach. You might also consider taking a 10-minute flight to either of these islands, which we were told will cost about $100 apiece but spare you the 60- or 90-minute ferry ride and the long waits to get aboard. Finally, if you go to Old San Juan, we strongly recommend you try Aguaviva Restaurant, where the food is to-die-for fresh. We loved the mahi and mango ceviche, the medium-rare tuna steak and the halibut. Do not miss the watermelon sangria. It's one of the best drinks we've ever had. HAPPY TRAVELING!!!!

<Author>philvirta
<Content>Good for a few days My wife and I stayed at the Fajardo Inn March 20-22. We rented a car and drove ourselves using the hotel's instructions. It was a little hard to find, but not too bad. At the final turn up the hill to the hotel, there was just a blue sign stating Inn, not Fajardo Inn (at least not that we saw), so watch out for that.The hotel staff were friendly and helpful. We had booked the 3 day, 2 night Sunset Package (or it could have been Sundown), that included a welcome drink, breakfast both mornings, dinner at Starfish Restaurant and dinner at the Blue Iguana Restaurant (both at the hotel). I would note that the restaurant vouchers both stated they were not good for steak, seafood, alcoholic drinks or the gratuity. The steak and seafood clause was not so much of a problem at the Blue Iguana Restaurant, where they had a variety of choices. But at the Starfish Restaurant, the steak and seafood clause really limited our choices.Our room was not ready when we arrived (mid-afternoon around 3 p.m.), even though the desk staff had told us it was. It wasn't much of a problem as the housekeeping staff was close to the room and had things whipped into shape in about 10 minutes. There is no elevator at the hotel (at least none that we found), so be prepared to carry your baggage up some stairs if you're staying in a 2nd floor room. I believe the staff would be more than willing to help you out if you needed it.The room we stayed in (2nd floor, main building) was clean and the bed was large and comfortable. The air conditioning worked fine, although we left it off at night and slept comfortably with the windows open. We had a small balcony from which we could see the ocean and some of the nearby islands. It also overlooked the parking lot, but this was not a problem. It was pleasant to sit out on the balcony at night on the two chairs provided in the room and enjoy the breeze. Our room also had a table, a large armoire, a small television with cable, a programmable safe, an iron and ironing board, a refrigerator and a very large mirror. The bathroom was clean and basic with a large tiled shower and a little shelf for toiletries. Housekeeping kept everything ship shape throughout our stay.We didn鈥檛 try the little pool on the property, but did go down to Coco鈥檚 Park, a big, family-oriented facility that鈥檚 just a short walk down a hill on the property. The swim-up bar was not in operation during our time there, nor was the whirlpool. There is a very large pool sufficient for swimming laps, should one desire, and a very large shallow pool (about 1 陆 to 3 feet deep) that would be great for kids. There is a decent waterslide and a nice little waterfall that kids should also enjoy. Coco鈥檚 Park also has a miniature golf course. Had we brought the kids, my 4-year old son probably would have loved the place and spent all his time in the pool or playing miniature golf. Towels for the pool were available in a little shack above Coco鈥檚 Park or from the front desk. Don鈥檛 lose them, as they will charge you about $20 to replace them.There is a gym on the property (Jaggery Gym I believe it鈥檚 called) that I checked out but didn鈥檛 use. At the time we stayed at the Fajardo Inn, guests would have to pay $5.25 to use the gym. The gym was well equipped with cardio machines, exercise machines and free weights. There was a fitness instructor on duty as well. Be aware that they do require you to wear tennis shoes if you want to use the gym (no sandals or flip-flops).The Starfish Restaurant at the hotel served good food. Even though we were on a meal plan, I will note the prices were a bit high. The service was a bit slow; expect to invest a couple hours to sit down and eat. I鈥檒l mention again that if you got a package deal with meal vouchers, you鈥檙e very limited in what you can eat at Starfish Restaurant; no steaks or seafood, which means you can have chicken or pork. My wife had chicken cordon bleu, which was very tasty and I tried chicken with onions saut茅ed in a rum cream sauce, also very tasty. We shared a large platter of Puerto Rican appetizers, all fried so not good for the diet-conscious, but delicious and fun to try something local. We had pi帽a coladas there which were good, but a bit on the weak side. Dessert was also good. I would pass up the starfish sundae and go right for the expresso (sic) cake. We also had breakfast at the Starfish Restaurant and I would recommend the a la carte menu as opposed to their limited buffet. If you鈥檙e just looking for a light, carbohydrate-rich breakfast, the buffet is for you. It had lots of bread and croissants, some yogurt, little cereal boxes (like you get for the kids), oatmeal (you have to ask for it) and fresh fruit. The a la carte menu had eggs (as you like them, omelette, or eggs benedict), french toast and pancakes. They also had sausage, bacon, ham, hashbrowns and juice. The coffee was decent and the service was marginally faster than at dinner.The Blue Iguana Restaurant offers a broad array of tex-mex dishes. I had to catch the attention of one of the kitchen staff to get some menus, but after that, service was efficient, timely and friendly. The barkeep (who also turned out to be our server) made a decent pi帽a colada and really moved things along when we let him know we had a tour date to keep that evening. The food was good and filling, although my fajitas were a bit on the greasy side. The quesadillas my wife had were good and there was more than enough food leftover to take some back to the refrigerator in the room. Dessert was good, but nothing spectacular; cheesecake with cherries and fried tortilla wedges dusted with cinnamon sugar.Overall, the Fajardo Inn is a nice place to stay for a few days. You can drive to nearby Luquillo beach if you鈥檇 like to get some sun  sand and it鈥檚 only about 20 minutes to El Yunque (Caribbean National Forest) where you can hike the trails to your heart鈥檚 desire. You are also very close to the ferries to Culebra and Vieques and just a short drive from Las Cabezas de San Juan park, where I would recommend taking a kayak tour of the bioluminescent bay on moonless or near-moonless nights. My wife and I took the tour with Yokahu Kayaks and they were very professional, friendly and made the tour fun.

<Content>A bit of Blah... Stayed at the Fajardo Inn for a 2 night stay with hubbie and 2 kids 7  4. All and all just an average place to stay, if you can't find anywhere else to stay, at least it was clean and not too expensive. I would probably not stay here again.

<Author>SN1752
<Content>Trying Too Hard A 2-day stay at the Fajardo Inn capped an 8-day circumnavigation of Puerto Rico. The property just feels like it's trying too hard to be something it cannot be. Its location on a hill keeps it from being a sprawling resort  its location in the country keeps it from being a prime destination. Not that it doesn't try to impress you with a large pool complex... it just seemed out of place, though. It would be like a Vermont country inn adding a high-tech cinema. It's not a bad property; it's just not comfortable. The property's web site indicates that the restaurant is a certified Meson Gastronomico but that must be outdated because there is no listing of it on the PRTC website that certifies the restaurants. The restaurant is pedestrian and overpriced, though they mix a good drink. This would be a passable property for a long weekend with a couple of kids, but that's about it.

<Content>Less than Impressed We were in Fajardo for approximately 4 days. Certainly, there is a lot to do in this area. Unfortunately they seem to have a monopoly in that area as the only other reputable place was El Conquistador - which, after speaking to a variety of other tourists, were less than impressed with their expensive stay there.

<Author>CouleeCat
<Content>A great destination in itself! The only challenge we had at this hotel was actually figuring out how to get to it. Once we did though, we were not dissapointed. We had booked one of the honeymoon suites ($135 per night) and it had a very nice view of the city, hills surrounding it and a bit of the water from our private balcony. The room was spacious, very nicely appointed, and the bed was firm and wonderful - the best we've slept in anywhere. It had a jacuzzi tub in the bathroom, which we never did use, wetbar, refrigerator and microwave. There were two pools and we spent quite a bit of time at the larger one. A little warning to those of you, like me, that seems to attract every biting insect within 20 miles, use a bug spray because I came home with over two dozen very itchy bites from the no-see-ums that hang around the pool. The water slide looked fun and I would've loved to go down it even though I'm a 50-something. We were surprised to find that the whirlpool was not a heated, but liked how it water-falled into the larger pool.The first night we had dinner at the Starfish. What a delight. We ordered the Puerto Rican sampler appetizer and enjoyed every one of the little deep-fried treats-the sauce that they served with it was the best we'd had in PR yet. My husband and I shared a Caeser salad with chicken and each ordered one of the pasta dishes and a side of rice and beans. Everything was prepared exceptionally well. We ordered chocolate cake to take back to the room for later and it was very decadent. Was that why I gained 8 lbs. in one week?!The next night we ate at the Blue Iguana at the hotel. Again, the meal was wonderful and priced reasonably.We loved the little gatos that roamed the property, especially the friendly little kitten that hangs around the lobby area looking for someone to play with (of course, many people happily obliged her). From our balcony, the sound of the coqui were a treat to listen to at night. This can be a very romantic place to stay but it is also great for families with children. Everything, including the very helpful front desk staff is first rate.

<Author>MyAdvice
<Content>Good place to stay to check out rainforest, biobay, or Vieques/Culebra I would rate this place almost a three diamond hotel; there are certain aspects of the rooms that make this place two diamond, but there are many aspects of this place that exceed what is found in a two diamond hotel. The Room:We stayed in the main building; in the main building the rooms with the odd numbers overlook the town area. The rooms with the even numbers have the views of the ocean. Our room itself, which was had two queen beds was huge; it was about 15x20. I can say that it was quite nice to stay at a place that you actually had more than 6鈥?between the side of the bed and the wall. The room had an in-room safe, a small refrigerator, a table suitable for eating on or working. One thing that was missing in the room was a microwave. The furniture was nice and modern, the beds were mushy soft and the bedspreads were a little worn. The TV was fairly small at 17鈥? The bathroom was a little dated, and had a shower stall instead of a tub. Overall, the room was acceptable and a little better than what I had expected. One more thing; do not turn on the AC and then leave the room for several hours. The AC is powerful and our room was quite cold when we came back. Since there was no heat in our room, we had to open up the windows to let the heat in!The Hotel: The hotel had a small business center and wireless access. Unfortunately, wireless could not be reached from the room; one had to go onto the front porch or lobby to have access. Fortunately, there were several tables/chairs on the front porch, so one could work there. The hotel staff was very friendly. Be sure to ask them for a copy of 鈥淨ue Pasa鈥?and 鈥淧laces to Go鈥? While I did not eat at the seafood restaurant at the hotel, it was a Mesones restaurant. Mesones is kind of like a seal of approval for restaurants serving authentic Puerto Rico Cuisine. The Mexican restaurant at the hotel was fairly inexpensive, but nothing to write home about. The hotel had two pools; the one by the hotel is a typical pool; the one over the hill (Coco鈥檚) is the one that you would expect to see at a resort. You need to check in at Coco鈥檚 guest house to visit Coco鈥檚 pool. They will give you towels at the guest house for use in the pool area. Be warned that there are confusing signs about the pool hours. I鈥檓 not sure when the pool was actually closed. There were signs at the pools that said the pool was open till 6:00pm; others that said 7:00 pm and the note on the door in the hotel room said 8:00pm. There is also a nice gym (with free weights) on site as well as a place to play mini-golf, tennis, and basketball. Also, as others have noted the hotel is very easy to miss. If you go to the one-way loop by the docks, you went too far. There is a sign that says hotel as other posters noted, however it is about a 12鈥漻18鈥?blue sign and very easy to miss. In case you miss the turn, the sign in the other direction was partially obscured by vegetation. The road that the hotel is on is a fairly wide road. I would guess that it is about 30-40 feet wide. Where to Eat/Shop:There are several American fast food and family style chain restaurants on route 3 between route 194, including McDonalds, Wendy鈥檚, Ponderosa and Sizzler. There is also a Wal-Mart, a few grocery stores, and a Walgreens in this area. Except for the Golden bagel and the restaurants at the hotel, there is very little commercial activity near the hotel, so I recommend renting a car to get around the area. Nearby Activities:If you drive down to the docks to take a ferry to Vieques of Culebra, there are gated lots that charge a parking fee of $3-5/day. The ferry docks are to the north. You can get the ferry for $2 per adult one-way. Purchase tickets across the street from the ferry dock. You do not want to take the ferry to these islands if there is a storm coming or if there are high winds as the water will be very choppy. Do not pick outside seats on the ferry unless you want to smell diesel exhaust for the one hour trip. The nearest beach to the hotel is the Seven Seas beach; it is quite easy to get to. There is also a bioluminescent bay in Fajardo near the Seven Seas beach.

<Author>Innovation423
<Content>Nice hotel in great location The Fajardo Inn is a great place. I would definitely recommend it and would go there again.The pool is terrific. Apparently the pool hours used to be short but they are now 8am to 8pm. There is free WiFi near the hotel lobby, which is especially welcome because of telephone connection charges in the rooms and the cost of using the business center鈥檚 computers. Bring your own laptop and enjoy all the Internet you want. The rooms don鈥檛 have clocks鈥攕o bring a travel alarm clock.People complain that the hotel is hard to find. One reason is that the location on the directions map of the hotel鈥檚 own website is wrong. This is the web address of a map that shows the correct location of the hotel: http://www.travelmaps.com/fajardo.html When you鈥檙e driving to the hotel on Carr 195/Calle Principal, look on the left for a government-style road sign that simply says 鈥渉otel鈥?with an arrow to the left. Turn left after that sign and you鈥檒l see the Fajardo Inn at the top of the hill. But there鈥檚 no sign that directs you to 鈥淔ajardo Inn鈥?anywhere, and no sign I could see that identifies the street as Parcelas Beltran.Incidentally, if you鈥檙e driving to the hotel from the airport in San Juan, I鈥檇 recommend that from Carr 26 you take Carr 66 (instead of Carr 3 the whole way) until Carr 66 dead-ends. Then you turn right on Carr 3 and follow the rest of the hotel鈥檚 directions. Carr 66 is a toll road which costs $1.50, but it鈥檚 worth it.About restaurants鈥攖he hotel鈥檚 restaurants are good, but assuming you want to try some others, let me recommend: The best seafood we found was at La Parrilla, which is Kiosk #2 in the long line of restaurants and bars in front of Luquillo Beach. All seafood restaurants, this one included, cost about what you鈥檇 pay in the continental U.S., so they鈥檙e not cheap at all. Rosa鈥檚 seafood is quite good and is much closer to the hotel (take the last right turn before the ferry port and go to the end of the street). Anchors Inn, which is on the way to the El Conquistador, costs slightly more and just wasn鈥檛 as good. Pasion por el Fogon, near Anchors Inn, is very expensive. There is an excellent Cuban restaurant called Metropol located in the shopping center with the movie theater at the intersection where you turn from Carr 3 to Carr 194 on the way to the hotel. This is a copy of the highly-regarded Metropol located in Isla Verde.Finally, the Golden Bagel restaurant, which is on Carr 195/Calle Principal just a few blocks before the hotel, is a great place. It has both traditional Puerto Rican and more continental U.S.-style breakfast and lunch entrees. The espresso is excellent, it has a range of bakery items, and believe it or not, the bagels are quite good. Free WiFi as well. We went back several times.

<Author>prOakland
<Content>We love it. Fantastic pool, nice clean rooms. The hotel is on a hill, so its a tough walk up to the lobby and down to the pool, especially if you have to drag luggage. However, if you have a car, you can park it right outside your door.We only stayed here to go on the East Winds snorkel tour to Cuelebra. They pick you up at this hotel for $14 per person so you don't need a car.This hotel is supposed to be only 1.5 blocks from the ferry, but it's staight uphill and the locals told us to take a taxi. The Taxi cost $20 for only a 3 minute drive, so I felt cheated.After the bad reviews about the food being bad and expensive, I was relieved that the food was pretty good and not that expensive. The average dinner at both restaurants was $7-$15. There's a refrigerator in the room so you can take leftovers back, but take a plastic fork to eat it with later. There is no microwave. If you need a taxi from here back to San Juan, I recommend Angel and Mary. They live in Fajardo, speak English, and are very punctual and reliable. I Reserved the taxi 1 day in advance. and cost $60 for 3 of us with luggage.I wished I could have stayed longer, just to relax by the beautiful pool. It had a water slide, waterfall, and crystal clear water that didn't smell of chlorine. Do not bring any valuables to the pool. There were 2 young, kids, around 9 and 14 years old, not guests, walking around and around the pool very slowly, looking at all the chairs as if waiting for you to get up and leave your things unguarded. If you wanted to swim after you checked out, there are showers and lockers by the pool. But you need your own padlock and the lockers are not big enough to hold your luggage.The mini golf was $2 per person per round. They give you really large, thick beach towels, but charge you $20 if you lose it.They have an internet room in the lobby. I think it was about $5 for 30 minutes. But if you have your own laptop, its free.

<Author>Zephyr-TA
<Content>Fajardo: Good Location for Exploration Stayed 3 nights, 12/14/06-12/17. We very much enjoyed our stay here. We arrived early and they prepared the room early for us including a portable frige! We found the desk staff to be most friendly and helpful. They provided detailed directions for us to a long list of questions, including directions to the Golden Bagel for great coffee and pastries! The room was a standard ($100/nightly plus taxes) on the main floor facing the pool, quite clean, quite adequate. They responded promptly to our requests for additional room needs. We visited the Mexican restaurant on several occasions and found service and food to be quite adequate. The Christmas decorations were beautiful! As noted by others, there's a bit of hill and stair climbing to do if using the front entrance. The landscaping is very nicely done. I'd stay here anytime.  And I also would consider staying here as a base to see other places like Old San Juan, the big park, 5 minute access to the Vieques  Culebra ferries, the day-trip sail boats, the casino across the harbor in the big hotel, where rooms are typically much more expensive. All of these easily accessed without the traffic of San Juan.

<Author>midgetmama
<Content>Pretty good minus the ants I paid $134.52 for a standard room with a balcony for my mother and I on 12/20. I think the price of the hotel is a bit high compared to others I could get in Puerto Rico for the same price.We spent a lot of time looking for this place, mainly due to bad directions we got from someone in San Juan. When we finally found it, it was very simple and easy to get to and from the hotel.There are a LOT of stairs here. If you're disabled, forget about it. They did have a few ramps going up, and I guess you could stay downstairs, but it would still be a very complicated journey to get to the front door. My mom and I are pretty active and packed light, so this wasn't a problem for us. There is no elevator, but the staff does offer help with your bags if you need it.The hotel had some lovely Christmas decorations, and the grounds are pretty nice. The girl working the front desk was not especially friendly, but she was efficient enough.The room itself was very plain, and when I went to turn on the air conditioner I found it surrounded by ants. I've never had bugs in any room I've ever stayed in (except the Penny Sleeper in Anaheim, which we left immediately), so that was a surprise and made me a little paranoid about climbing into bed that night when I returned and found them gone. There was also some kind of bug in the shower that never moved.We did have a great view of the water and El Yunque and listened to the coqui the whole night.We took the bio-bay tour with Yokahu Kayaks, and when we returned the Starfish restaurant had already closed, but we had planned to go to Blue Iguana anyway, which is open until 11. You have to pay for chips and salsa, which we did. They were good but not spectacular. I got the chicken taco combo, and my mom got quesadillas. Everything was delicious, but the beans were a little too Tex-Mex for my liking. For all this and free refills on the soda, it only cost $19, making this our cheapest meal after the Luquillo beach kiosks.Check-out was easy, and there turned out to not be any bugs in my bed.For the most part, I really did like the hotel, but I think certain staff members could use a little improvement, and the bug problem wasn't pleasant. The whole bathroom also just seemed a little grungy. It's a good and convenient place to stay but slightly overpriced.

<Author>LAKaren
<Content>Not what we had expected We stayed during the Christmas holiday after spending a wonderful week on Isla de Vieques. The hotel was pleasant enough at first, but then things got pretty bad. We had a room with 2 full size beds. After the first night, my husband was getting bitten by some sort of bug. I don't believe they were bed bugs. We spoke to housekeeping, and they said they would change the bedding  bedspread. This did not help. My husband asked to change rooms, and they wouldn't comply. They said they would change the mattress. This didn't happen. So after the 2nd night of being bitten up, we asked to change rooms again. The people at the front desk said they couldn't do this. It was only after we mentioned Trip Advisor, they finally agreed to change our room. After that the bug bites stopped. The hotel is pleasant enough for the price but be advised there is alot of walking to be done. There are no elevators but is is only a 2 floor hotel. We were traveling with our young children, so if you forgot something in your room, it's up the steps. It's also a distance to the washer  dryer, and if you use the larger pool with the slide next to the mini golf course, it's another LONG walk and a full flight of stairs down to the pool.So if you have a problem with stairs or traveling with small children, you may want to think twice! The staff was very pleasant but we started off on the wrong foot. We ate breakfast out at several different bakeries. Most served some sort of egg sandwhich or french toast (for the kids). It was cheaper than eating in the hotel restaurant. For dinner, try heading down to the seaport where there is a road lined with many restaurants.
