<Author>Longwood Traveler
<Content>Great Find and Excellent Service I booked two standard suites at the Fajardo Inn for my son and his wife and myself and my partner. I was very happy with the choice of this hotel not just because of the price (which was very reasonable) but because the service and the amenities were just right. No this is not a luxury property but it is clean (sheets are changed every day - you don't even get that at the Marriott), the people are helpful and friendly, the pool (only one was open at the time) was huge and entertaining and the restaurants and bar were well priced and appetizing. The drinks are more than fairly priced and they aren't stingy with the liquor but they do caution about overindulging.Our two suites cost less than $150 per night and were located in a separate casita so it was like we had our own separate hideaway. The king-sized bed was comfortable but don't expect to see a lot of furniture in the room. It had a full kitchen and the bath was okay. The only problem we had was with ants (not unusual in the Caribbean and since we live in Florida something we are unfortunately used to). When I mentioned it to the front desk on the way back from breakfast to my room, she said she would have housekeeping get on it right away. She wasn't kidding - the housekeeping staff got to the room before I did and sprayed the place. Since my son had the upper room in the building and didn't have any ant problems I would recommend staying out of the lower level rooms if this is a problem.The Starfish restaurant was very nice and we ventured out to a few of the local places such as the Anchor Inn and the Conquista and had nice meals at both places. The hotel is very convenient to El Yunque and Luquillo Beach and if you forget something there is a Walmart in town.We also used the Internet service and that worked fine for a quick check of e-mails.Overall a great place for the money. We'd go back there again.

<Author>csjobert
<Content>Not bad at all This place was surprisingly good for the value. It's not on the beach but is a short ride away from the beach. There are two pools one in the main section and one by the new section with slides into the pool overlooking a beautiful landscape. It even has a swim up bar and dining areas. The restaurant does include two restaurants and bar. I would not recommend this place for the elderly or the handicapped because the hotel is located on a hillside and you have to walk quite a bit just to get to the rooms and some going up hill or downhill. There are no elevators. Every thing is located on various levels (bars, restaurants, pools etc.) The rooms are pretty roomy and very clean and include a small refrigerator. The staff was very kind and helpful. If you can't stay at the big resorts nearby, this is your next best bet with a great value.

<Author>happycook
<Content>Strongly disliked the place I can't give the Farjardo a terrible rating because it wasn't an evil nightmare, it just made me profoundly relieved we had only booked one night and I had great sympathy for the staff - they couldn't just flee like we could!Ironically, the place looks rather impressive in a fancy schmancy way, then your soul is slowly sucked out by the surreally dreary, impersonal rooms, the counter-productive attempt to limit pool time (guests nervously edging around the early evening pool closed sign as if fearing they might be yelled at) and the ghastly Mexican microwave food at the cheaper hotel restaurant. We timidly asked if we could buy tennis balls (like, to use on the tennis court?) and might as well have been demanding to purchase ski boots!It's by no means a nasty place, the sun shone, the pools were lovely - when open - but thank goodness it was only a stop-gap stay. You creep away with a lighter wallet and no special memories whatsoever.

<Author>humanone
<Content>Best place to stay in Fajardo Although there are two mega resorts around Fajardo, and some funky inns, the best choice is the parador Fajardo Inn. There are a number of room choices, all fine. Ours had a view over the smaller swimming pool onto the sea and mountains; we were on the second floor. The room was big and clean, and the airconditioner perfect. But...when you arrive ask for a map of the property. It was only on our last day that we discovered the new huge pool with spa and water slide, next to the putting green and children's playground. The price was reasonable, $95 for weekday, $114 for weekend. However, the two restaurants are merely adequate. Dine instead at either the Anchor Inn or Pasion por el Fogon (passion for the wood stove like grandma used). Eat at any road side stand and try each of the typical Puerto Rican fried appetizers.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Best Bargain In Puerto Rico This has to be the best bargain in all of Puerto Rico, in fact, it is probably the best bargain in all of the Caribbean. We stayed at this resort with two other couples April 1st - 4th prior to taking a cruise. I will say that this hotel is very much hidden and a little tricky to find, but worth the extra effort to track them down. Our rooms were wonderful, clean and quiet. The pool is fantastic and even though they had limited hours (6PM) we were never asked to leave after 6PM and in fact one evening we stayed till nearly 8PM with no problems. We did utilize our own BYOB at the pool and were never hassled even though the sign reads no food or drink; however we were discrete about this. The Mexican restaurant was not bad..the pricing was good. The upstairs restaurant was VERY good and the staff was outstanding and very accommodating. Breakfast was pricey and so after the first day we went down the street to a typical local restaurant, the food was fabulous and the prices were very inexpensive. I will have to say that the staff at this hotel was very friendly from the moment they assisted us through directions to the hotel on our cell phone to the day we left, they were fantastic. If you go to the front desk you can get full size beach towels and only need to sign for them, they never asked for a deposit. The beach towels were clean and of good quality, in fact we took them with us on a snorkeling trip. The front desk staff was helpful with giving us numbers to local tour groups and was very good at giving directions to local beaches. The hotel had a few problems, but the price of this hotel was so good I won't even mention them.One of the best things about this hotel is that you are only about four miles from a huge mega-resort the El Conquistador were our husbands had a great day golfing and we spent one evening having dinner and enjoying the casino. Just as an example the El Conquistador was at least $250 more per night than the Fajardo Inn. I recommend staying at the Fajardo Inn and enjoying a quiet, clean hotel with a mega-resort pool and a Holiday Inn price!! We can't wait to return!

<Content>Beautiful resort atmosphere As a family of four, we spent three nights at the Fajardo Inn. We occupied the family room, a room with three double beds. The room was huge! <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>We had a good time! We stayed at the Fajardo Inn for one night. The rooms are plain but they served their purpose. The grounds are well maintained. The cleanliness of the room was so-so but I wasn't skeeved like I was at some of the other places we stayed in Puerto Rico, such as The Great Escape Inn in Vieques and The Howard Johnson in Isla Verde. The pool was awesome. It is huge and has this huge hottub and swim up bar. The pool hours are from 9am-7pm. It closed way too early. And we went to the restaurant right near the desk with the big boat in the front and the bar as soon as you walk in. I forget the name of it but I told the waitress I was a vegetarian and she brought out fettucini alfredo made with chicken broth. How disgusting!! Who would put chicken broth in alfredo sauce? She didn't listen to me when I ordered. Would I stay there again? Maybe. Compared to the other hotels I stayed at on my trip, this one was paradise.Incidentally, while we were in Fajardo, we went to the airport and flew on Vieques Air Link to Culebra. The flight was 15 minutes late but it was amazing. You can see all of Fajardo, Palominos Keys, and Culebra from the air. The flight was an unforgettable part of our trip. We didn't have any of the transportation problems on Culebra that we did on Vieques. We called Kiko's Transportation Services and he took us to Flamenco Beach. He was wonderful. I highly recommend his services! And Flamenco beach is the most beautiful beach I have ever been on in my entire life. My fiance' is 6 feet, 3 inches tall, and I took a picture of him standing in the water up to his shoulders. You can see his feet in the picture. That's how clear the water is. And my fiance loved the pinchos (BBQ chicken on a stick served with a roll) that they sell on Flamenco Beach. I loved the Pina Coladas. They were orgasmic. If I went to Puerto Rico again, I would stay on Culebra.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>not the place to go for peace and quiet Spent three nights here in March. The Farjado Inn is physically very nice-beautiful views, inviting lobby, polite staff. That being said, the longer I stayed the more I could not wait to leave. The huge beautiful pool has ridiculously short hours. when we did find time to lay by the pool one afternoon we walked away with our ears ringing--from 10am to noon they were pressure washing the pool (very loud!). When that finally stopped it was replaced by the soothing sound of dump trucks, cranes, construction and the very loud stereo of the construction crew directly behind us. Yes, the huge pool is adjacent to a huge construction site.I would have retired to my room for a bit of peace and quiet, however directly oustide of our room was a large table saw. They seemed to be building closet doors and doing miscellaneuos carpentry the whole length of our hallway for the duration of our stay. For days after we left everything in our suitcases smelled like mold (the general aroma of our room).The food also left a lot to be desired. There was absoletuly no consistency, and there is only one restaraunt open for lunch which is entirely mexican food. never did find the jacuzzis. when i called to ask the front desk where they were they replied that the jacuzzis were not currently open and that they are never open unless the hotel is at maximum capacity.

<Author>dunewalker
<Content>Peaceful, Clean, Such a Deal! The Fajardo Inn was as clean and sweet as the Puerto Rico country air and a true escape from the touristy beat. Having stayed in upscale hotels in San Juan and Dorado on previous visits to PR, we had decided to sample a simpler style of lodging. Puerto Rico really has enchanted us (married couple in 50s), and we felt that we should see if the magic held up without the four-star safety net. Our 3-day, 2-night stay in the Fajardo Inn in early February was definitely not long enough and we are eager to return. In fact, staying at the Caribe Hilton in San Juan for the next six nights, we drove to the Fajardo vicinity two more times! (That can take more than an hour each way.) Driving in from the airport, we had no problem finding the highway turn-off for the Inn and once we knew where it was, it was equally easy to find it at night. From previous reviews, we were a bit leery about reports of steep stairs and sparse rooms. But we unloaded the trunk of the rental car in the driveway, and by the time my husband returned from parking, the manager had carried our luggage up to our room via the beautiful sweeping staircase. And so it went. They knew us and looked out for us cheerfully. Service was impeccable, without the sometimes too-closeness of a BB. THE ROOM. We stayed in a 鈥淪tandard room w/balcony鈥?in the main building. There was a tiled floor, small refrigerator, phone, cable TV with stations from the States, a cafe table and two chairs, dresser drawers, two night tables, your regular sliding-door size closet and a roomy queen bed that allowed us to sleep like babies. The bathroom had a huge shower w/soap and shampoo supplied, and since we don鈥檛 expect Egyptian cotton bath sheets at those prices, we were satisfied with what we got. The air conditioner was just fine. I would have liked at least one upholstered chair to sit in. My husband didn鈥檛 care. The small BALCONY immediately overlooked some parking spots, another low-rise Inn building and a variety of evergreens and palm trees. In the distance was a view of green hills and the town of Fajardo with El Yunque looming behind it. In the other direction was the not-so-far-off Atlantic with a view of Culebra Island and smaller cays. Not bad for $95/night.THE POOL AND GROUNDS. As a pool aficionado, I was pleased. Yes, the pictures of the larger pool complex look like a computer-drawing on their web site, but it really does look that way in person! The pool bar wasn鈥檛 open on weekday afternoons, but the wonderful layout of the large pools, the beautiful landscaping, green hills and violet skies, and various birds, iguanas and some wandering, friendly cats and roosters kept us relaxed and entertained. The original pool 鈥?a nice-sized, deep rectangle in a courtyard aside the hotel 鈥?also was surrounded by all kinds of palms and evergreens, and by extremely friendly guests, many of whom were return visitors. The pool towels, which you get from the front desk, were top of the line!It鈥檚 not hard to see why the Inn has received environmental awards because it鈥檚 so creatively landscaped. In the public areas and hallways, you鈥檒l pass a lot of original art, some folky, some not original, but all nicely and imaginatively framed. The colonial island architecture of the main building was welcoming. Everything was designed with an extra, caring touch.OTHER SERVICES. The service staff was terrific and there was always someone cleaning the public areas. When we called for extra towels and TP, room service came immediately. I couldn鈥檛 get a dial-up Internet connection for my laptop in the room. When I finally went to the front desk they said they only connect the phone if so requested, and when I complained that I had wasted precious time, they gave me a free (usually $5) half-hour stint in the two-computer high-speed Internet room. There is a laundry room for the guests.RESTAURANTS. For breakfast and dinner, the Star Fish restaurant was good but not memorable (our full-breakfast selections were about $8 each; dinner main courses, mid-teens). The Blue Iguana bar and grill (w/pool tables and a large screen TV for viewing sports) was generous for lunch and dinner with a wide variety of home-made Mexican food that hit the mark for about $7 and up. Wine and liquor was fairly priced. You could eat entirely on the ground for several days and be neither bored nor broke.ENVIRONS. You鈥檒l do best to get a rental car at the airport, because you will want to explore the surrounding area, including the nearby rainforest, sweeping Luquillo Beach, the bioluminescent waters, etc. Staying entirely on the Inn鈥檚 premises, despite their two affordable and pleasant restaurants, might be just a bit too quiet for more than a few days. Since the Inn is NOT on the beach, you鈥檒l have to drive there. It鈥檚 fun to explore the unpretentious restaurants down by the marina and along the main road to the Inn. At the turn-off from Highway 3 are several shopping centers, with fast food chains and a large Walgreens offering any drinks, snacks and sundries you might need.For some reason, I couldn't transmit photos w/this review, so just know that the Inn's website photos don't do it justice. <Content>A little piece of paradise... Just an hour鈥檚 drive from the airport, the Fajardo Inn is a peaceful East Coast respite from the hub-bub of the metro San Juan area. We have been vacationing at the Inn for over a decade and with the recent completion of the enormous pool area with its water slide, swim up inpool bar and whirlpool area, kiddie playground, miniature golf and banquet facilities, the Inn has truly evolved into a comprehensive destination for family fun. For sports enthusiasts-- tennis and basketball courts, and a fully equipped gym are near completion. Can鈥檛 live without your computer --- take it with you for free WiFi access in hotel鈥檚 lobby or use the Inn鈥檚 computers for a nominal fee.The guest rooms have been refurbished with new mattresses, linens, furniture and paint. Golf courses are a short driving distance if you enjoy the game. Access to the Culebra/Vieques Ferry is minutes from the Inn. The trip to these out islands with their beautiful white sand beaches is a must for any visitor interested in a quiet, unspoiled setting. (Best time: weekdays). Although the two on-premise restaurants are adequate, there are many off-site eateries that also offer excellent meals at reasonable prices.We consider our five weeks spent at the Inn most enjoyable. Spending days in each of the Inn鈥檚 two pools working on our tans, exploring the area, golfing, snorkeling, kayaking, walking and watching the sun rise over Culebra and set over Yunque provide a powerful reminder of nature鈥檚 wonders here in Puerto Rico. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved the Fajardo A great value... the pools are great - clean and nice. The staff was friendly and helpful with questions and the rooms were clean, nice furniture but basic. I enjoyed the grounds as well. You can't beat the value at this place. I didn't eat in the restaurant but saw the breakfast buffet -- didn't look healthy (i.e. premade muffins in wrappers!) Also, you can probably sneak onto the El Conquistador boat and island if you just tell them that you are staying at the hotel... they want to see your room key but tell them you forgot it and to look your name up on the list... when the don't see it they will probably just let you onto the boat rather than make an issue out of it... plus if you buy any food or drinks on the island it will more than offset the cost of the boat ride that you stole! Loved farjardo, the inn and the nearby beaches. Keep in mind that there aren't a lot of restaurants nearby and they seemed overpriced -- 20-28 an entree which weren't remarkable.

<Author>BQ74
<Content>Just OK... We stayed at the Fajardo Inn for 4 nights. The good parts about the hotel are the price (reasonable for the area), the family-friendly pool area, both restaurants have good food at reasonable prices, the staff is friendly, there are nice views of the ocean and the mountains, it is very close to the ferry for Culebra and Vieques, and they help coordinate excursions including bioluminescent bay kayak trips (which are also close by). There were a few bad things that would make me reluctant to recommend this hotel. The rooms are very sparse and dismal (not even an alarm clock, with tile floor and fluorescent lights). I did not feel comfortable relaxing there in the evening. The bed was uncomfortable with bed-bugs. I woke up several times during each night itching and in the morning saw many new bites--not from mosquitoes or sand fleas, definitely from some insects living in the bed. The staff did not communicate very well with the excursion companies. I suggest arranging tours yourself and calling to confirm the status of the tour the night before or day of, in the case of the night bioluminescent bay tour (so cool!) instead of relying on hotel staff. Overall, this hotel seems on-par for Puerto Rico and for the price you pay per night.

<Content>Nice, comfortable hotel, value for money My husband and I stayed 3 nights at Fajardo Inn and the overall experiance was very nice. The rest of the room was nice, with comfortable beds, chairs and a shower-only bathroom. The inn has 2 pools - the bigger one with the swim-up bar is really nice and we spent a lot of time here. The bar and food at the Blue Iguana (one of the hotel's restaurants) was really good. The hotel does not provide complimentary breakfast, and we had to spend $7.50 for a very ordinary breakfast everyday, that most other hotels offer for free.You will need a car to visit places while staying at Fajardo Inn. We made trips to El Yunque, Luquillo Beach and Seven Seas Beach. The best trip we had was with Las Tortugas Tours - a dusk thru' night kayaking trip through mangove canals and into the Biobay Lagoon. We didn't want to goto Vieques, so we toured the biobay just off Fajardo, which is reportedly almost as nice.We really enjoyed our stay at the Fajardo Inn - away from the crowds at San Juan, while being close to many attractions.  
<Date>Dec 28, 2005

<Author>elba
<Content>very very nice Fajardo Inn, Fajardo Puerto RicoJune 16, 2005tripadvisor member, Mahopac New York WE stay at the Fajardo Inn June 3rd thru June 9th, and we loved the Inn the minute we step off the rental car. The Inn is situated on a hill so you will have a view of the rain forest El Yunque in the distance as well as an ocean view. This place is great if your planning on visiting Vieques or Culebra, two tiny islands on the east coast of Puerto Rico.  There are two restuarants on location One serves typical Puerto Rican dishes, great rice and beans, excellent mofongo ( plantain spicy dish with meat of your choice ), the other serves Mexican food, good Margaritas. The Inn has only two floors, our room was located on the second floor. The room was nice, comfortable bed and soft pillow. It had a tiny balcony. There's no clock in the rooms and theres no elevator so if you have problems going one flight up book a room on the first floor. The pool was great, plenty of sitting chairs surrounded by tall palm trees and tropical greenery. The inn is located one hr. from San Juan. We arrived late Friday in the afternoon so we hit heavy traffic. IF you choose to stay at the Fajardo and are landing in San Juan choose an early flight landing to avoid the traffic. There are great Places to visit in hte near by location. Our main reason for choosing the fajardo Inn was the great Price. We went to culebra island and visited flamenco beach. If you are a beach lover you need to see flamencos waters. Crystal clear with many shades of blue and green. The ferry seaport is located 5 mins away cost four dollars. The Inn gave us great info. They told us to vist Culebra during the week, to avoid larger crowds. We went on a Tues and it was truly perfect. We had a great time Our stay was so enjoyable that we are palnning our next years return trip to Puerto Rico, and the Fajardo Inn is on our list. ElbaSid, New York

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Diamond in the Rough The Fajardo Inn is a baby in Hotel years, but its not suffering from growing pains. The hotel has beautiful architecture with even more beautiful interiors. The hallways that lead to the rooms on the main building are elegance at its finest, they're decorated with beautiful paintings and are accentuated with soft lighting, not something I expected from a little hotel such as this. We stayed on the second floor and all those people aching from the no elevator complaint are just nitpicking, frankly there's about 20 stairs and if that takes the wind out of you, perhaps you should work out. We had no trouble getting our luggage up the stairs due to the fact that we asked for assistance just like the sign by the stairs indicated. The staff was more than happy to assist.The two restaurants, Starfish and The Blue Iguana, while small, are just what the hotel needs. Frankly we've stayed at larger hotels which only had one restaurant and we were amazed when we found out this one had two. (Note: While there we inquired about the Sea View Bar and were told that it was currently under renovations and would open in June) The food at the two restaurants was better than expected. One minor complaint about the Blue Iguana is that they have all these TVs but their volumes are always on mute. What's the point? The only one that had sound was the big screen located behind the bar.There were no activites to peform while we stayed there, but then again they never claimed to have any in the first place so its not a surprise. The location was close enough to all the tourist attractions we went to so it wasn't a chore to go to them. I suggest doing the bioluminescent bay at night, its truly a marvel.Overall, it was beyond our expectations and most of the complaints we read here prior to our visit were unfounded. I wouldn't allow isolated incidents to spoil a visit to this diamond in the rough.

<Author>BostonIndian
<Content>Nice Place We stayed there on 3/31 - our first of four nights (see reviews for Trade Winds in Vieques, El Buen Cafe in Hatillo and Marriott Resort in San Juan)The place is pretty easy to find if you follow the directions on the website. The only place it gets confusing is the left turn a few blocks before the hotel (we missed it and ended up at the ferry harbor/port). Had to get directions at the Post office!The hotel - It's a sprawling complex. We had the honeymoon suite. The room was nice and clean, with a refrigerator and A/c. Nice views from the balcony - the ocean on one side and El Yunque on the other.The Blue Iguana had good food... good drinks too.The breakfast buffet was really well priced $7.50 for the quality of food there (everything from fresh fruit to yogurt, danishes, bread, juices, bagels etc)The bulk of the construction seems to be done, so it was not noisy during the entire stay. The new pool at the lower level was amazing in it's landscaping, but was still not open. The upper level pool was refreshing and clean.The staff is helpful. They knew the area. Parking was not a problem either. We actually left our car there since we were making a trip to Vieques and would not have returned till the next morning, and I was not comfortable leaving the car in public parking spots.The ferry is a 15 minute walk from the hotel. Make sure you give yourself ENOUGH time - at least 90 minutes before your scheduled ferry departure if you have not gotten tickets yet (actually I don't even know if you can buy advance tickets). I had to wait 45 minutes at #2 position in line just because all tickets were sold and the ticketing agent was waiting for confirmation on a block of tickets that could be released (hence leading to my assumption that you probably could reserve blocks of tickets)The airport is about 10 minute ($10 for the two of us) ride too.(we took the ferry to vieques and the flight back to fajardo... in case you are wondering :)The bad stuff - we did not have hot water (we had barely tepid/warm) till late in the evening. That was a let down since I had reserved the room because of the jacuzzi. My girlfriend accidentally discovered that hot water's on around 6 PM. So, it was not a total disappointment.

<Author>Luv-2-Cruise
<Content>Perfect Location (..AND GREAT MARGARITAS!!) Frankly, the hotel room itself is not what you come to this hotel for. There are, however, many many other assests that make it worth staying at while in Fajardo.#1. The location is unbeatable if you are around town to visit El Yunque, Luquillo's beaches, or are going to Vieques/Culebra for a day or a weekend visit (it is minutes from the ferrY and the hotel provides a van for $3/person to take you there, so you don't have to mess with the taxis). #2. The rooms are large and the A.C. is great! There is also a small fridge in the room to keep your water cools, which is a nice plus.#3. The views from the Ocean View rooms w/ small balconies are very nice, particularly when you can turn your head to one side an see the blue/green ocean and turn your head the other and see the tremendous peaks of El Yunque's rainforest with clouds nesteled at the top.and.... #4. Last, but certainly not least, is the GREAT AND INCREDIBLE AND RATHER UNBELIEVABLE Margaritas at the Blue Iguana Restaurant on the property.My boyfriend and I are from Texas, so we've had some great margaritas in our lives.... but, let me tell you, these rival any I've had in Texas or Mexico, for that matter. The food (Crown Nachos w/ chicken and the Tortilla Soup) was great... but what truly stole the show was the Margaritas (and the Medalla beer- the local Puerto Rican beer- is also worth mentioning).All in all, the Fajardo Inn gets 2 thumbs up from us!! We truly enjoyed our stay!  
<Date>Mar 30, 2005

<Content>Great and getting Better My wife and I just returned on Tuesday from our first trip to Puerto Rico. We spent two nights in the Fajardo Inn and loved it. <Author>SZ
<Content>a good base for the area I thought the Inn was a very good value, having paid the same for a lot less in other areas of Puerto Rico. I stayed there primarily to go to Luquillo Beach, to kayak through the mangove at night to the bioluminescent Laguna, to visit El Yunque and to eat at the seafood restaurants in the Las Croabas vicinity. We ate one breakfast and one dinner at the Starfish Restaurant which were good, but not exceptional. You can't compare it to the nearby resorts because it is a modest operation and you pay accordingly. The grounds are beautifully landscaped and tended. We did see two cats while there but were not bothered by them. And the bedsheets did pop off of the mattress. The room was very large and we turned off the airconditioning every night. It was always very pleasant returning there after the day's or evening's activities. If you want something that will entertain you day and night it is not the place to stay but if you want a very nice accomodation while pursuing interests in northeastern Puerto Rico I would highly recommend it

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Inexpensive Spanish style resort hotel A bunch of travellers were unexpectedly detoured to this inn due to the blizzard in the US. It turned out to be a really pleasant surprise. The hotel is modern, with an open spanish style lobby and styling. The rooms were large and well kept. The pool was right next to the hotel but private and luxurious. Two restaurants and a sports bar inside. The staff was a little overwhelmed by the sudden surge in guests, but was helpful and friendly. It was close to a luxury resort, but much more inexpensive.Please note that there is a small companion building with very spare basic rooms adjoining (the former hotel before they remodeled) called the Scenic Inn which cannot be recommended. Also the surrounding area of Fajardo is a little run down. Still this was a real treat, and I wouldn't hesitate to return and relax!

After trying to get a hold of the front desk by dialing zero and getting no answer, we had to get an outside line and dial the hote's main number. I had to go to the front desk and ask for a manager, which was not very helpful either. She just apologized and that was it. Our package had two dinners included, and even though the site says that the dinners do not include alcoholic beverages, when we got there we found out that it does not include sirloin, T-bone, or seafood The restaurant staff made us feel very uncomfortable and cheap when asking these questions too. Other than that, the hotel per se is nice.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The Good, The Bad, and The Ugly Good: at $65.00 per night, it's very affordable (we stayed in the scenic inn). location wise, it's very attractive: minutes away from Culebra beach ferry, El Yunque Rain forest, Luquillo beach, and the phosphorescent bay. the pool is sweeeeet and plans for a new, much larger pool (with swim up bar) is in the works. in-room a/c units are arctic class. tv offers nice channel selections like HBO, Showtime, and Cinemax. Iguana Bar/Mexican restaurant is terrific. the main hotel and hotel grounds are beautiful. the staff was generally very friendly. Bad: nothing to do! the hotel makes a zero effort in making the place lively. pool and restaurants/bar close TOO early. one, count it, ONE ice machine on the entire premises. NO telephones, clock radios or remote control for the TV, so forget a wake up call, listening to music and/or lying in bed watching tv. the Starfish restaurant (for seafood) is God awful. a little salt and pepper goes a loooooong way. carefull with the towels and room key! $50.00 replacement charge for EACH missing towel, $200.00 for losing the key! Holy S--T! and yes, they make you sign out for EVERYTHING! UGLY: cats! behind the scenic inn lies a cat burrow. we counted atleast 12. they tend to roam freely at night, and are always fighting. room had an ugly ceiling stain (water damage?) and the towel rack always fell off. no attempts from the hotel to remedy both. the awesome balcony of the scenic inn (if set-up properly) is nothing more than a mattress storage space. we found one in the hallway, just next to our door. it's as if they don't care or, its a result of poor hotel management. avoid room number 10 of the scenic inn. all the other rooms have coffee tables w/ chairs, tv stand/drawer combo and ample living space. number 10 looks like a converted closet. the poolside restrooms and main lobby restrooms could use something called a urinal scented cake. cheap and effective. whoa. Summary: you get what you pay for folks! truthfully, i was pleased most of the time. my thing is this: if they have the resources to build a new and impressive pool, then surely they could address the other minor issues. if they got it together, they would be a force in the Fajardo area hotel wars. my experience aside, when in PR, just have FUN!

<Author>Nycbunny
<Content>Cute  The Fajardo Inn is a little tricky to get to... make sure to pay attention to the road signs on the side of the road.. otherwise you'll end up at the marina... just as I did. LOL!I was really surprized how well kep this hotel is maintained ( in  out) considering that this is a 2 star hotel. Yes, the hotel has no elevator... but this can be a good thing .. since you may want to shed pounds after all the Puerto Rican food you'll eat!!!! It is fantastic ! The pool is sparkling blue.. The view from the hotel is amazing .. to the west ..you can easily see El Yunque.. and the misty clouds that surround it .. and to the east the Atlantic. I stayed in a basic room that overlooked the pool, and the only complaint that I have is the mold scent that came from the a/c unit. Just ask for lysol from the room steward and you'll be fine. The room is spacious, and it included cable.. which is nice! The room service for breakfast was speedy.. and the food is delicious! There is no extra fee for parking which is always a plus... and yes.. rent a car!!!! The staff is so friendly, and never hesitated when I had a question. It's the Boriqua hospitality that makes the Fajardo Inn charming ! If you can afford the Conquistador .. go for it ... but if you want the best bang for your buck stay at the Fajardo Inn.... They are only 10 minutes apart .. but you'll be saving much more at the Fajardo Inn!!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Staff is pleasant until they receive your money.... My friend and I chose the Fajardo Inn on our last night on the island because of it's proximity to Fajardo Beach, the phosphorescent bay, the ferries to Culebra/Vieques, and it's view of the island. The reviews about how the staff are rude and ration out bath cloths/towels like you are in prison.... were right on. There's no elevator and because the building sits on a hill, 2nd floor rooms are a real climb. I must say - the idea of the Fajardo Inn far surpasses what you actually get. Staff is pleasant until they receive your money (which is taken at check in).... then they show their true colors. The upper staff are on a power trip and don't hesitate to let you know. The inn is overpriced for what you actually get, even moreso since it is at least 40 minutes from San Juan and the airport. Also, when you check out - be sure not to leave anything in your room. The hotel will hold it hostage and take their time letting you back in to get it for you. We found that out the hard way. Never have I been treated so poorly nor had so much trouble to check out of a hotel. My favorite part of my stay at the inn was relaxing in the pool and being 5-10 minutes away from the beach. If staying in Fajardo, I would recommend looking for a different place to stay. I know I will next time.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The main inn is beautiful, but the desk clerk was dreadful I have seldom had more bizarre treatment by a hotel desk clerk than our experience at the Fajardo Inn. We had reserved a room via the Internet at The Scenic Inn, the lower-priced inn next door to, and run by, the Fajardo Inn. Our rate was $60 for two people. When we picked up our rental car in San Juan, we had picked up a brochure for the Fajardo Inn, printed only in Spanish, that advertised rooms for $55. We could only translate part of what the brochure said, but it looked like it should be available to us by the dates printed on the brochure. Upon check-in, I produced the brochure and asked the clerk for the advertised rate, but he said that the discounted rate was not available on weekends. We accepted that and went to our room in The Scenic Inn and found that the air condtioner had a sign on it not to use it and to see the desk clerk. So we went back and the desk clerk acted a little put out, but he did change us to another room in The Scenic Inn. This one was huge and had a working air conditioner, but it had a television set that only received one channel and it had a ridge on the cement floor that one could stumble on (it must be where they removed a wall that was there at one time). The room would have been tolerable at the $60 price, given the overpriced nature for the qaulity of what you get in Puerto Rican hotels in general, if I had not realized at that point that it was not in fact a weekend (it was Thursday) and so we should have been given the $55 rate in the brochure I had picked up (unless the real reason it was printed only in Spanish was so that the offer would not be available to us Gringos). I went back to the desk clerk and told him that I had realized that it was Thursday. He insisted that the offer was not available on weekends or holidays. (This was not a language problem - he was quite fluent in English.) I said, It's Thursday. This is not the weekend and it's not a holiday. He disappeared into the back and talked to someone and came out and said that the $55 offer was only good for a room with one bed in the main inn and not in The Scenic Inn. I said that that would be fine since we only needed one bed and the rooms in the main inn were much nicer than The Scenic Inn anyway. He disappeared in the back again and talked to someone and came back out and said that he was sorry, but the system was down, so he could not tell if there were any rooms available in the main inn. When we persisted that, surely, he could tell if there was an empty room without the computer, from the keys or the registrations or something, he said that if we would wait an hour until the system came back up, he would find a room in the main inn, and then come and inspect the room he had given us in The Scenic Inn and, if he found that we had not used the bathroom or the sheets, he would switch us to the main inn. At this point we were pretty sure that he was just jerking us around so it was becoming a challenge, and since we wanted a beer anyway, we went to the bar and had a beer and then went back to the desk when the hour was up. He said it would be 10 more minutes before his system came up. We said that would be okay, that we would go get our bags from The Scenic Inn if he was sure he was going to have a room in the main inn for us. Some miracle must have occurred just then because he could suddenly punch stuff into the computer although the system was supposed to be down, and he was able to tell that there was in fact an empty room in the main inn. When we appeared with our suitcases, he did give us a key to a room in the main inn, but he said that he could not give us the $55 rate instead of the $60 rate we had booked at, and that we would have to see the manager in the morning if we wanted the $5 difference. Once we finally got to a room in the main inn, it was beautiful - all gleaming white tile and perfectly clean. We never did go back in the morning to try to get the $5 discount the brochure promised - we were just grateful to have gotten out of the dumpy Scenic Inn and into a nice room. The room in the main inn was terrific by Puerto Rican standards, especially in the under $100 price range, which seems to be pretty universally dumpy throughout Puerto Rico. But we sure had to work to get them to deliver on what they advertised in their brochure that we picked up in the rental car agency.  
<Date>Feb 3, 2004
